Huai River Development Committee Plans to Open a New Canal 23

Plan to be Proposed at the Liang-Huai Reclamation Conference

(Nanjing) The Liang-Huai Reclamation Conference is scheduled to be held on the 15th at the Ministry of Industry. The Huai River Development Committee will send its Chief Engineer Xu Kai to attend. Mr. Xu also has a plan to open a new canal in Liang-Huai. The plan includes: opening expenses of $36,000; surveying expenses of $1,000; measurement costs of $20,000; construction costs for the first phase, building ship locks and earthwork at Doulonggang and Chenjiagang, $300,000; totaling $2,066,600, to be completed in two years. The second phase, including water gate bridge culvert maritime engineering and other recurring expenses, is tentatively budgeted at $3,000,000. The entire river is 270 kilometers long. The cost of planting saplings along the dikes is $36,000, and the contingency fund is $120,000. The total estimated cost is $8.3 million. The benefited fields are estimated at over 300 kilometers in Chenjiagang, totaling over 13.8 million mu. The funds for land purchase, etc., for the first phase of the project are estimated at $2.8 million and should be raised first. The second phase is planned to be financed by collecting benefit donations and land reclamation fees in the area where the first phase of earthwork is completed. The average levy is $2 per mu, to be paid in five annual installments, with each mu paying $0.40 per year, yielding an annual revenue of $786,000. There are also 2.025 million mu of barren and developed land, with an average levy of $1 per mu, also to be paid in five annual installments, with each mu paying $0.20 per year, yielding an annual revenue of $405,000. The total revenue in five years would be $2,025,000. The total revenue from both sources would be $5,955,000. If payment is overdue, the land will be purchased at the price before the new canal is completed. Developed land will receive a subsidy for land reclamation. 80,000 mu of wasteland along the river will be purchased to build new towns. Subsequently, the land price will naturally increase, and it will be resold at $20 per mu, totaling $1.2 million when fully sold. West of the Fanggong Dike, where the new canal will be built, there are approximately 12 million mu. Excluding the 4.05 million mu within 10 kilometers west of the new canal, there are still 7.95 million mu. A levy of $0.08 per mu per year would yield an annual revenue of $636,000, totaling $3.18 million over five years. The total estimated revenue above is $10.335 million, which is sufficient to cover all construction costs with a surplus. (Special dispatch, 13th)

Feng and Pei Counties Attempt to Block River Mouth 25

Construction to Begin October 1st

Fears of Escalating Disputes

(Xuzhou) Feng and Pei counties are planning to block the Dasha River mouth. After opposition from Xiao and Dang counties, Tongshan County has also started to oppose it. Representatives from Feng and Pei counties held a joint meeting in Feng on the 9th. Present were Feng County Magistrate Yang Liang, Party Secretary Li Futing, Pei County Magistrate Hu Zhaohe, Party Secretary Tang Tongshu, and representatives from both counties. They decided to form a dike repair committee to block the two river mouths at Gaozhai, with construction scheduled to begin on October 1st. 8,000 laborers will be deployed daily, and the project is expected to be completed in half a month. A request will be submitted to the province to send personnel for inspection, and cooperation from Yutai and Teng counties will be sought to strive for the closure. The interests of Feng and Pei counties conflict with those of Xiao and Dang counties, and each is drawing support from counties with similar interests, which is likely to escalate disputes. (Special dispatch, 13th)

Araki Proposes National Policy Plan

Japanese Political Situation Suddenly Becomes Tense 26

War Minister Says "Manchuria Problem is Above All Else"

Emphasizes the Necessity of Strengthening National Defense

Frequent Contacts Between Cabinet Members in Recent Days

(Tokyo) The issue of establishing national policy by the government has suddenly become tense since War Minister Araki presented the military's research on national policy and actively participated in the issue. The government is waiting for the government to take active action due to the internal and external situation and the current state of rural areas. Meeting with representatives of both the House of Peers and the House of Representatives, it obtained a unified national opinion to implement the national policy. However, simply sitting idly by would only cause more anxiety. Therefore, just as it was forced to implement the national policy that was due, the sudden proposal of the War Minister's important national policy greatly moved all aspects of the political world.

On the 9th, he met with Finance Minister Takahashi and Vice Minister Shigemitsu, representative of Foreign Minister Uchida, to discuss important national policy proposals. Naval Minister Osumi and Finance Minister Takahashi exchanged important views on national defense national policy and ideological education economic finance issues. Thus, the national policy issue is extremely tense, and cabinet members are frequently traveling and meeting. The War Minister has now resolved to submit the national policy to the cabinet meeting after obtaining the understanding of the cabinet members, in order to implement the most serious emergency national policy. (Japanese Allied Press dispatch, 13th)

(Tokyo) When War Minister Araki met with the Finance Minister and the Prime Minister, he explained the urgency of the international situation and emphasized the necessity of strengthening national defense. He also presented the military's private proposal on national defense financial resources, stating that an extraordinary tax increase of about 50 million yuan could be implemented from the ninth year. With this as interest, another 1 billion yuan in special accounting military bonds could be issued, which would not be mixed with deficit bonds. If the repayment period is forcibly extended, 1 billion yuan in financial resources could be obtained. The Prime Minister and Finance Minister both replied that although the extraordinary tax increase of about 50 million yuan is set aside for now, the strengthening of national defense is necessary and should be considered with a permanent financial source, issuing special accounting military bonds. The issue of financial resources for military expenses will become a political issue and will be discussed by the cabinet. (Den-tsu dispatch, 13th)

Outline of Araki's National Policy Plan 27

(Tokyo) At 9:30 AM on the 9th of this month, War Minister Araki visited Finance Minister Takahashi and had a confidential talk for three and a half hours. The Japanese political world regards this as an important meeting, and it is rumored to be a preparatory work for the military to actively control the political situation. If its opinions cannot be accepted by the government, the military may seize power. However, its content remains secret. According to the outline reported by the Tokyo Asahi Shimbun on September 10, it is as follows:

Manchuria Problem 28

Regarding the Manchuria problem, I (Araki self-proclaimed) have already explained its current situation to the Emperor. The most urgent issue for Japan at present is the Manchuria problem. Even if we abandon everything, we must seek the healthy development of "Manchukuo." This is the most fundamental national policy. All other national policies should arise from this. The actual situation in Manchuria in the past two years seems to be reforming various systems and developing industries with the force of a bursting river, gradually proceeding according to the planned plan. The public security is also almost the same as before the incident, and the soldiers of the Sixth Division can return to defense. Taking advantage of this opportunity, we must redouble our efforts in industrial development, and the results can be expected.

China Problem 29

After Song Ziwen returned to China, key figures of the National Government gathered in Lushan to discuss and study various important domestic and foreign issues. Although China is currently eager to change its policy toward Japan, its domestic situation may not allow it to change. Japan's fundamental policy toward China has always been to maintain friendly relations between the two countries. If the method is not right, it will be manipulated by China. We must be very vigilant and quietly observe its general trend. Regarding emergencies, all relevant agencies should earnestly connect and cooperate to deal with them.

Foreign Relations 30

The world situation may not be favorable to Japan after its withdrawal from the League of Nations. If China abandons its diplomacy of using barbarians to control barbarians, it is difficult to expect its rapid improvement. Moreover, 1935 and 1936 are imminent, and the naval treaty and the time of withdrawal from the League of Nations are all coming. At this time, when Japan's naval power is relatively inferior to that of Britain and the United States, a crisis in East Asia will come. Japan fears that it will encounter unprecedented national disasters. In today's international situation, which is difficult to improve, expanding national defense is essential to maintain peace in the East. The navy is eager to implement the second replenishment plan, which can be said to be a natural requirement. In order to prepare for Russia and China, the army should prepare a strong army. This is the best way to maintain peace. It should not be plagued by financial and technical problems and leave harm to the future. Foreign policy should aim for 1935 and 1936, and should be consistent with the outside world.

Education Problem 31

Japanese education after the Meiji era has indeed developed across generations, but recent education is mostly education for the sake of education, forgetting the education needed by the country and the people. Communist Party members also come from the proletariat and illiterate classes, but many have received higher education, which is due to shortcomings in our education. Therefore, we must create Japanese people who can understand the unparalleled Japanese national essence. The basic restoration of education to this spirit.

Ideological Problem 32

Due to the shortcomings of the education system, ideology is affected, which has been described above. There are also many reasons for promoting ideological deterioration in political and economic organizations. Such shortcomings can be corrected to a certain extent by the power of politicians. Therefore, we must overcome all difficulties and seek to renew all administrations. In short, Japan must make "Manchukuo" sound and developed, and at the same time, it must break the current national difficulties. At this time, politicians, educators, and knowledgeable people in the private sector must unite to solve it. In order to achieve this goal, the government should first decide on a national policy and do its best to implement it. War Minister Araki said after the meeting that what is needed at present is only to act decisively. (China United Press dispatch)

Five-Year Fuel National Defense Plan 33

Minister of Commerce Acts as a Lobbyist for the Military

(Tokyo) Minister of Commerce Nakajima visited Prime Minister Saito this afternoon at 1:00 PM to explain the content of the Five-Year Fuel National Policy Plan. At 2:30 PM, he continued to visit Finance Minister Takahashi for the same explanation, and requested understanding for the 6 million yen needed in the first year. Finance Minister Takahashi said after the meeting that the fuel national policy was decided by the committees of the former ministries, and the navy also sent a committee member. Because it is absolutely necessary for national defense, it will be investigated as one aspect of strengthening national defense. (Den-tsu dispatch, 13th)

(Tokyo) Japan believes that the world situation is very urgent. Once a war breaks out, the fuel for warships, tanks, aircraft, and various traffic institutions depends on foreign supply, which is very dangerous for national defense. In order to solve this problem, the Ministry of Commerce and Industry, the Army and Navy, and the Resources Bureau (the main agency for economic mobilization planning) organized the Fuel National Policy Coordination Council to earnestly study countermeasures. After two deliberations, it was found that the opinions of the Ministry of Commerce and Industry and the Resources Bureau differed greatly from those of the military, and it seemed difficult to compromise. Later, due to the urgency of the budget submission period, the Ministry of Commerce and Industry succumbed to the military at a meeting on September 8, and drafted a five-year plan based on the military's plan, with a budget of 26 million yuan to complete this project. The initial year's budget is set at 4 million yuan. Here are a few of the military's main points: (1) Vigorously support the research of liquefied coal to make this invention practical and help its enterprise; (2) Help the modified alcohol industry to replace kerosene. This raw material, such as molasses, is very abundant in Japan, and it will not be frustrated halfway in an emergency; (3) Actively support the mining area of ​​the Sakhalin kerosene test excavation and increase the kerosene production; (4) Use the natural gas of the Jinshui oil field in Taiwan to manufacture gasoline; (5) Assist the existing fuel companies to develop their business; (6) Negotiate with Britain, the United States, and Russia to import oil. (China United News Agency Communication)

The Japanese Ministry of Foreign Affairs has the following views on this: (1) The move by the League of Nations General Assembly to discuss the Sino-Japanese issue again is probably because the Chinese side believes that even if this opportunity is missed once, the meaning of not recognizing the puppet state is equivalent to interruption, which puts the Nanjing government in a difficult situation internally. From this point of view, it may have plans to appeal to the League of Nations again; (2) Although the League of Nations adheres to the principle of not reviewing the same matter again, there are the Rehe issue and the North China issue after the recommendation was adopted, which can be a new content for the appeal. Therefore, if China appeals in this way, the League of Nations will have to accept it; (3) However, Japan has already occupied Rehe by force, and a satisfactory ceasefire agreement has been established with the Chinese side on the North China issue, and there is no need to bother the League of Nations again. Moreover, if there is no risk of war between China and Japan, there is no room for the application of Article 16 of the Covenant. Even if the Ministry of Foreign Affairs does not send representatives to attend this General Assembly, no matter what the content of China's appeal is, it will not feel any pain. Cuba's New Cabinet Established, Situation Remains Bleak 43

Retired Military Officers Yet to Yield

US Declares Retention of Right to Intervene

Havana: Although Cuba's new cabinet has been formed, it is reported that unless the faction of former President Miguel Mariano Gómez Menocal can be persuaded to join or at least adopt a position of tacit support, a new revolution will brew. Today, as the new President Grau San Martín formed his cabinet, he invited all factions and revolutionaries to support it in order to strengthen its power and prevent American intervention. However, former President Miguel Mariano Gómez Menocal and Céspedes are unwilling to support this "government of scholars" and are adopting a wait-and-see attitude. Although Céspedes is currently neutral and has not agreed to join the banner of anti-government forces with the three hundred-odd military officers who were recently ousted, Gómez Menocal does not wish to comment on the new government, stating only that he cannot honestly support it and predicting that the new government may not last for a week. However, he also indicated to his friends that he does not wish to be president himself, knowing that it would be difficult to please all factions and at the same time completely satisfy the United States. It is noted that although Gómez Menocal has never taken any action against the United States, he was not well-received in Washington due to his increased spending and taxes during his term.

Today, the new Cuban President appointed Sterling as Secretary of State, Arlanzo as Commander-in-Chief of the Navy, Sampol as Secretary of Labor, and Boteler as Secretary of Justice. Sterling is an experienced diplomat and journalist who was appointed as ambassador to the United States by Céspedes and has a good relationship with the Americans. It is said that the Cuban President's appointment of Sterling as Secretary of State is intended to gain American favor. It is noted that Sterling was also among the representatives when the Platt Amendment to the US-Cuba Treaty was discussed in 1901 and vigorously opposed the inclusion of the amendment in the treaty and the Cuban Constitution. It is heard that Sterling currently believes that even if the Platt Amendment can be abolished in the Cuban Constitution, it will be difficult to remove it from the treaty between the two countries or from the minds of people in Washington at this time. It is reported that US Ambassador Welles plans to visit Sterling tomorrow, and it is expected that the Platt Amendment will be discussed.

Havana: The four hundred Cuban military officers staying at the National Hotel are currently refusing the new government's ultimatum to submit immediately. The new government has issued a harsh ultimatum, ordering these four hundred officers to change their attitude within thirty-six hours, otherwise, drastic measures will be taken. However, this threat is not taken seriously by the officers. They have set up obstacles and made other preparations to resist any violent actions by the government. They insist that Dr. Céspedes must be reinstated as president and refuse to obey the orders of the new President San Martín. It is noted that the National Hotel is currently sheltering many American family members who sought refuge there during the revolution, so the hotel is under the protection of American warships' guns. (Reuters dispatch, 12th)

(Washington) Today, American officials solemnly declared that although the US government wishes to avoid intervention in Cuba, it wants to vigorously retain the right to intervene. The current situation in Cuba seems to have raised the issue of the existence or abolition of the Platt Amendment in the Cuban Constitution. News from Havana indicates that the new Cuban government is advocating for the removal of all provisions in the new constitution that recognize the special rights of the United States. However, from the standpoint of national defense and the large commercial investments in Cuba, the United States believes that the Platt Amendment must be retained. Therefore, it is anticipated that regardless of any action taken by the new Cuban government, the United States will retain the right to intervene. It is noted that the Platt Amendment was originally an amendment to the US Army budget bill in 1901. It was subsequently added to the Cuban Constitution as an annex before the transfer of governance to Cuba and stipulated in the treaty between the two countries. Now the new Cuban government is demanding the complete abolition of this clause recognizing the right of the United States to intervene in order to achieve full sovereignty. (National Telegram, 12th)

Shrinking the Earth 50

In the Past, It Took Three Years to Circumnavigate the World

Today, It Only Takes a Little Over a Week by Plane

Reuters New York Correspondence: Since the invention of the airplane, mankind has acquired the art of shrinking the earth. In the past, it took one thousand and eighty-three days to circumnavigate the world; today, it has been reduced to a little over a week. Historically, those who circumnavigated the world include Magellan, who led five ships with a total of two hundred and eighty people on September 20, 1519, from Seville, Spain, of which only the Victoria, carrying thirty-five people (excluding Magellan), successfully returned in three years minus twelve days. In 1577, Sir Francis Drake's expedition departed from Plymouth, England, returning in one thousand and fifty-two days. In 1586, Thomas Cavendish departed from the same location, reducing the journey to seven hundred and eighty-one days. In 1889, female journalist Nellie Bly, using New York as her starting point, circumnavigated the world by steamship and train, taking seventy-two days, six hours, and eleven minutes. She was the first traveler of the new era. In 1913, Mills also departed from New York, completing the entire journey in thirty-five days, twenty-one hours, and thirty-six minutes. Later, there was the magnificent feat of circumnavigating the world by airplane. Initially, it was accomplished by several American military airplanes in 1924 in one hundred and seventy-five days, but the actual flying time was only fourteen days and fifteen hours. They departed from Seattle, passing through Alaska, the Aleutian Islands, the Kuril Islands, China, India, Constantinople, Budapest, Paris, Glasgow, Reykjavik, Greenland, Labrador, Boston, and returning to the starting point. In 1925, Evans and Wells completed the entire journey in twenty-eight days, fourteen hours, and thirty-six minutes, traveling across mountains and seas, using both airplanes and boats. They first traveled by boat to France, then by airplane and train to Yokohama, then by boat to Seattle, and finally by airplane to New York. In 1929, the Graf Zeppelin airship departed from Lakehurst, New Jersey, USA, and circled the world in twenty-one days, seven hours, and thirty-four minutes. In 1931, Post and Gatty, piloting an airplane together, set a record for circumnavigating the world in just eight days, fifteen hours, and fifty-one minutes. This can be said to be fast. Even this year, Post broke his own record in a little over a week. Those who come later surpass those who came before, and the progress of the future is truly limitless.

Ministry of Finance Believes That Import Tax on Foreign Coal Cannot be Increased 64

(Nanjing) Regarding the previous request from the industrial sector to increase the import tax on foreign coal, the Ministry of Finance believes that, based on the principle of tariffs, there should be no difference in treatment between Chinese and foreign merchants. All shipments abroad will be subject to export tax, and those sold domestically will be subject to transit tax, in accordance with the tax rate. Although the mineral tax cannot be implemented uniformly at present, when a mineral tax is levied on all domestic mines in the future, regardless of Chinese or foreign capital, the principle of equal treatment should still be followed, without discrimination. Restoration of North China Armies to Pre-War Status 83

Reducing Total Military Expenses by 571,000 Yuan Monthly

Northeast Generals Decide to First Implement Eliminating the Weak and Retaining the Strong

Results of the Meeting of the Ping (Beiping) Military Council

Beiping Correspondence: Since the outbreak of hostilities in Hebei and Rehe, the North China armies expanded their troop numbers and reorganized into army corps. Consequently, the troop strength of each army increased by more than one-third compared to pre-war levels. After the end of the war, the Chahar Incident erupted, leading to a further increase to ten army corps. According to the North China military expenditure budget, at least 5.5 million yuan or more was needed monthly. The total local tax revenue was 2.5 million yuan. Under these circumstances, the central government subsidized 2 million yuan monthly. After offsetting income and expenditure, there was still a deficit of 1 million yuan. Although it was decided that military expenses would be disbursed at 80%, with each 36 days considered a month, there was still a monthly deficit of 700,000 yuan. After Finance Minister Song Ziwen returned to China, the central government, considering the enormous military expenditures in North China, decided to find ways to reduce them and instructed He Yingqin to be responsible for consulting with the generals in the area. After receiving the central government's order, He Yingqin telegraphed all the generals to come to Beiping and scheduled a temporary meeting for 9 a.m. on the 11th at Jurentang Hall. Army corps commanders Yu Xuezhong, Song Zheyuan, Pang Bingxun, and others, after receiving the order, arrived in Beiping one after another on the evening of the 10th and exchanged views at Jurentang Hall once that evening before dispersing late at night.

At 9 a.m. on the 11th, the temporary meeting of the Military Council was held in the grand auditorium of Jurentang Hall. Attendees included Yu Xuezhong, Shang Zhen, Song Zheyuan, Wan Fulin, Pang Bingxun, Jiang Bocheng, Xiong Bin, Bao Wenxue, Ye Biliang, Xie Jianyuan, Shen Zhenrong, Chen Qinruo, Gao Guizi, Liu Duoquan, Wu Ke'ren, Huang Shaohong, Qian Dajun, Hou Cheng, Qin Dechun, Xie Gangzhe, He Zhuguo, Wang Yizhe, Wang Shuchang, Rong Zhen, Liu Yifei, Zou Zuohua, Hu Yukun, Gao Weiyue, Ji Yiqiao, Men Zhizhong, and more than twenty others. Sun Dianying and Shen Kejun sent representatives to participate. The meeting opened at 9:40 a.m., chaired by He Yingqin. First, Shen Zhenrong, head of the ninth group of the Military Council, reported the detailed amounts of expenditures of each army and the current income and expenditure situation. Subsequently, He Yingqin stood up and spoke, stating that the total military expenditure in North China was currently 5.5 million yuan monthly, while current income was only 2.5 million yuan. The central government had to subsidize 2 million yuan monthly, totaling 4.5 million yuan, which still left a monthly deficit of 1 million yuan. Now, to address this deficit, the army must be reduced. He hoped that the leaders of each army could understand the difficulties. The standard for reducing troop numbers should be based on the company unit, with each company reducing at least twenty to thirty soldiers. He also hoped that each army could earnestly implement this. After He Yingqin finished reporting, he presented the two plans drafted by the ninth group of the Military Council. One was to reduce 700,000 yuan, and the other was to reduce more than 500,000 yuan. After the generals expressed their opinions one after another, it was decided that due to the short time, a detailed discussion could not be held, so it was decided to continue the meeting in the afternoon. The meeting temporarily adjourned at 12:30 p.m.

Because the morning meeting failed to reach a concrete decision, He Yingqin summoned the heads of the second and ninth groups and important personnel from the staff office at 1:30 p.m. to inquire about the actual income and expenditure situation of the North China military expenses. At 3 p.m., the meeting continued, with the same attendees as before. After the meeting resumed, the chairman consulted everyone's opinions. After mutual research, it was decided to announce the passage of the second plan to reduce 500,000 yuan. The reduction method was as follows: (1) The Northeast Army, consisting of the four armies of Yu Xuezhong, Wang Yizhe, Wan Fulin, and He Zhuguo, would reduce 30 soldiers per company, reducing military expenses by 400,000 yuan monthly. After the army reduction, the unit would still be restored to the division level. (2) For the four units of Sun Dianying, Song Zheyuan, Pang Bingxun, and Shang Zhen, apart from Pang and Shang's units, which met the original troop numbers, Sun Dianying's unit would reduce 40,000 yuan monthly, and Song Zheyuan's unit would also reduce 31,000 yuan. Together with the Northeast Army, the total reduction would be 571,000 yuan, which was almost equal to the current deficit. Finally, two decisions were made: (A) The number of divisions and brigades to be reduced by each army would be detailed in a table prepared by the highest-ranking officers. (B) At the regular meeting on Wednesday this week (the 13th), further thorough research would be conducted, and it was decided to organize a Finance and Supervision Committee. All opinions had been unified and would be implemented after being submitted to the standing committee. Subsequently, the meeting discussed the army training methods and adjourned at 5 p.m.

Regarding the issue of troop reduction and cost-saving for each army, a decision has already been made. It is now verified that in terms of cost-saving, the Northeast Army has been reorganized into divisions, with each division reducing 31,000 yuan monthly. The 32nd Army under Shang Zhen will reduce 25,000 yuan monthly, the 40th Army under Pang Bingxun will reduce 18,000 yuan monthly, the 41st Army under Sun Dianying will reduce 40,000 yuan monthly, the 106th Division under Shen Kejun will reduce 20,000 yuan monthly, and the 84th Division under Gao Guizi will reduce 900 yuan monthly. The total cost reduction for these armies is 574,900 yuan monthly. After this reduction, the total monthly expenses for each army are estimated to be 4.8 million yuan. Based on the monthly revenue of over 2 million yuan in North China and the central government's subsidy of 2 million yuan, there is a monthly shortfall of several hundred thousand yuan, which will be made up by the Military Council. In terms of troop reduction, the Northeast Army will reduce one machine gun company per regiment and one infantry company per battalion, totaling four companies per regiment. Each company will reduce 31 soldiers. In addition, a Finance and Supervision Committee will be established, with the responsible officers of each army serving as members to ensure financial transparency. A Training Committee will also be established, with regulations drafted by Qian Dajun, Shang Zhen, Rong Zhen, Zou Zuohua, Men Zhizhong, and ten others. Once the drafting is completed, preparations will be made for its establishment.

The generals of the Northeast Army, due to the decision made on troop reduction and cost-saving measures, found it necessary to decide on implementation immediately. Therefore, at noon today (the 12th), they convened at the private residence of Wang Yizhe, commander of the 67th Army, to discuss the method of starting the reorganization. Wang Yizhe, He Zhuguo, Liu Duoquan, Wu Ke'ren, Zhou Fucheng, and others attended. As a result of the discussion, the steps for downsizing have been decided. Each army will first eliminate the weak and retain the strong and then receive military pay according to the established regulations. If there is still a shortfall, they will request the central government to provide subsidies. (September 12th)

Difficult Restoration of Shanxi Party Affairs 84

Former Provincial Committee Member Liang Xianda Assaulted

Tongmeng (Alliance) Faction Members Still Active

Beiping Correspondence: According to those who recently came from Taiyuan, Shanxi Province, since the conflict between the provincial party headquarters and the student petition group in the winter of the year before last, which resulted in the death of Mu Guangzheng, a student of Jinshan Middle School, resulting in a tragic incident, the party affairs of the entire province have been in a state of stagnation. The various party committees are located in Beiping, Tianjin, Nanjing, Shanghai, and other places, with Beiping as the general hub. The mass movement in Taiyuan is being led by public associations organized by student unions, etc., as substitutes. After the Mu Guangzheng incident was resolved by the Kaifeng District Court, calls for the restoration of the party headquarters were heard from time to time. After several visits to Taiyuan by representatives sent by the central government for consultation and multiple mediations by Zhao Pilian and others, it was advocated that the old provincial party headquarters, the Datongmeng (Great Alliance) faction, and the reorganization faction should negotiate a mixed organization. However, due to factional relations, each refused to yield, and no agreement was reached. Recently, most of the old provincial party committee members believed that the situation had eased after a long period, so propaganda minister Liang Xianda and others returned to Taiyuan one after another. It is heard that Miao Peicheng, a member of the Central Committee who is most watched by society, has also arrived in the province. The student union is again opposing the arrival of Miao and others and has posted slogans all over the streets to overthrow and eradicate various "red" and "green" elements as a preliminary movement of demonstration. Unexpectedly, a strange drama of Liang Xianda being assaulted occurred during the demonstration. It turned out that Liang was having a haircut at a barber shop in Liuxiang on the afternoon of the 8th when he was suddenly spotted by a few students. While one side monitored him, the other side sent someone to summon their comrades to strengthen their momentum. In an instant, the students had gathered dozens of people. First, two people entered the barber shop, pointed at Liang, and asked if his surname was Liang. While Liang was still denying it, they dragged him out and surrounded him with the crowd. They pulled and tugged him to the memorial monument of Mu Guangzheng in Zhongshan Park, forcing Liang to kneel on the ground and asked him if he was the murderer of the tragic incident, as if in a trial, not allowing him to reply. Then, the crowd punched and kicked him, subjecting him to assault. At this time, the Public Security Bureau heard the news and sent police to rescue him, and the perpetrators fled in all directions. Liang was sent to Shanxi Hospital for treatment by the police. It is said that Liang suffered serious injuries to his waist and the skin had turned purple. According to Liang, his return to Taiyuan was by order of the central government and he was not the only one. As for the tragic incident, it had already been resolved by the Kaifeng Court. This assault was truly unexpected. Since this incident occurred, all sectors of society have paid close attention. The authorities especially convened a military and political meeting this morning (the 9th) to discuss countermeasures. Public Security Bureau Chief Chen Shurong personally asked Yan Xishan and Xu Yongchang for instructions. Yan and Xu both advocated handling the matter according to the law. After receiving the order, Chen sent personnel to arrest the student perpetrators, but they had all fled upon hearing the news and could not be found. Chen Shurong also considered that it would be inconvenient for Liang in Shanxi Hospital and planned to ask him to go to a hospital run by Westerners in Fenyang or Taigu for recuperation, but Liang refused and decided to file a criminal lawsuit with the court immediately. How the party tide in Shanxi will be resolved seems difficult to predict. It is said that Minister of Interior Huang Shaohong, who came to Taiyuan recently, had discussed specific measures. There are even those who say that Li Guanyang, the leader of the Datongmeng faction, is about to go abroad and the old provincial party headquarters will be restored. Whether this is true or not is also unknown. (September 9th)

Chairman Chiang Kaishek Promulgates Guidelines for Relief of the People 85

Instructing All Armies Suppressing Bandits and Provincial Governments to Comply

Correcting Errors of Harassment and Abuse of the People

Nanchang Correspondence: During Chairman Chiang Kaishek's stay in Lushan, he planned to suppress the bandits, transform the military and political system, and review the shortcomings of the past army, paying particular attention to gaining the faith of the people and actively providing relief. He would then proceed to cooperate with the people. In his successive speeches, he also stated that suppressing the Red bandits was a war to win the people, not comparable to simply attacking cities and breaking enemies. Recently, he also promulgated eight guidelines for relief of the people, ordering all armies and provincial governments to comply. The main points are as follows: (1) Security of Life: Providing the people with protection against Red bandits, local tyrants, and the army. (2) Relief for Families: 1. Strictly prohibiting the forced occupation of civilian houses and destruction of civilian residences; 2. Not allowing the forced borrowing of civilian goods. In case of necessity, they must be returned responsibly; 3. Not allowing the extortion of rice, straw, or forced purchases of any goods from the people; 4. Not allowing the raising of funds, fines, or compulsory sales of goods from the people; 5. Not allowing the insult of the people and respecting their dignity. (3) Labor Relief: All previous corvée labor practices are strictly prohibited. (4) Production Relief: Protecting farmers' farming, plowing cattle, harvests, vehicles, livestock, and rural cooperatives, and finding ways to lend farmers plowing cattle, seeds, and small business capital. (5) Relief from Hunger and Cold: Making every effort to provide relief to disaster-stricken areas and refugees. (6) Construction Relief: Divided into the protection of highways, embankments, telephones, forests, etc. (7) Educational Relief: The army must not reside in schools, promote rural primary schools and basic education, and political workers must participate in education work as a duty. (8) Relief for People in Bandit Areas: One should be compassionate, appease the people in the bandit areas, and there must be no abuse or illegal acts inflicted upon the people. (September 11th)

Zhang Qun and Others Telegraph Request to Resist Dumping of Foreign Rice 86

This Year's Rice and Wheat Harvest Abundant, Sales Increasingly Sluggish

Levy Import Duties on Foreign Rice to Save the Precarious Situation

Hankou Correspondence: This year, the rice and wheat harvest in Hunan and Hubei provinces has been abundant, but sales have been sluggish and prices have been falling. In addition, the intrusion of foreign rice has had an impact. As a result, cheap grain hurts farmers, which has become a common phenomenon in the Yangtze River area. Zhang Qun, Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Government, went to Hunan at the beginning of the month to visit He Jian, Chairman of the Hunan Provincial Government. In addition to discussing the aftermath of the bandit areas and cooperation in water conservancy, this was also discussed. After obtaining the consent of the authorities of Henan, Anhui, and Jiangxi provinces, they jointly telegraphed the central government a few days ago, requesting the implementation of additional import duties on foreign rice and wheat to save the precarious situation. Chairman Chiang Kaishek has also paid attention to rural relief. A few days ago, he telegraphed the Hunan and Hubei provincial governments from Lushan, instructing them on the direction of agricultural relief and ordering them to send representatives to a meeting in Jiangxi to discuss the details. After receiving the order, the Hubei Provincial Government ordered the Civil Affairs, Finance, Construction, and Education Departments to each select one experienced rural affairs expert and researcher. These officials would then decide who would represent the province at the meeting in Jiangxi. Chairman Chiang Kaishek's telegram has been previously reported. The telegram from Zhang Qun and others is as follows: "Last year, harvests were abundant everywhere, and the yield of grain and rice increased sharply. At the same time, foreign rice and wheat were imported for dumping. This year's customs reports show that the quantity of imports has increased compared to last year. As a result, inland warehouses are overflowing, and there is no way to transport and sell the grain, which has a huge impact on the rural economy and social finance. We previously telegraphed requesting additional import duties on foreign rice and wheat in order to raise the price of Chinese rice, but it has not been implemented. Now, the new grain season is upon us, and the harvest is abundant again, while there is still a lot of grain stored from last year. Sales are increasingly sluggish, and prices are falling. Cheap grain is hurting farmers to the extreme. The cost of all the farming expenses needed by farmers cannot be covered by the price of the grain. Farmers regard their own profession as a dangerous path, and the fields are abandoned, and hidden dangers are emerging. Even industry, commerce, education, and national and local tax revenues are mutually affected because the source of income has been exhausted. Our country is based on agriculture. Foreigners' industrial and commercial aggression is already difficult to resist. If this agricultural product is also harmed by dumping, how can the people bear it? Looking ahead, we are heartbroken. It is essential to stabilize society by encouraging agricultural achievements. If the people are to farm, grain prices must increase. If no action is taken now, it will inevitably lead to collapse. Therefore, we specially telegraph earnestly, requesting the immediate implementation of additional import duties on foreign rice and wheat to resist dumping and save the precarious situation. We anxiously await your order." (September 11th)

The Trend of the Hankou Postal Strike 87

Party, Government, and Military Authorities Continue Efforts to Mediate

Municipal Government Orders Union Not to Take Action Beyond Regulations

Zhao Shusen and Others Arrive in Hankou to Discuss Responsibility Issues

Hankou Correspondence: The postal strike in this city is not likely to expand due to the continued mediation by the party, government, and military authorities. The postal workers' union has recently submitted a report on the situation to the provincial and municipal governments, stating that "The union was approved for registration by the municipal party headquarters, which provides a legal basis for it to be a legitimate organization. The union has requested recognition from the postal authorities, but has received no response, which has greatly hindered the union's work. Moreover, the treatment of workers at the Hankou postal bureau is far worse than that in Shanghai, and there is even more hostility towards the responsible comrades of the union. All members of the union are indignant and cannot bear it any longer. After convening a representative meeting, representatives and all executive and supervisory committee members were elected to request the municipal party headquarters to send personnel to negotiate with the postmaster, requesting written recognition of the union and requesting subsidies for union staff on a monthly basis, as is the case in other postal workers' unions, to ensure the protection and convenience of union staff. Union leaders should not handle bureau affairs, and all workers should be treated equally as in the Shanghai bureau. In addition to the earnest implementation of the proposals, we request the municipal party headquarters to send personnel to negotiate together. Therefore, we have prepared a document for reporting." After receiving the report, the provincial government telegraphed the central party headquarters and the Ministry of Transportation again to discuss a unified method and resolve the matter quickly to avoid further escalation. The municipal government also instructed the union, stating that "The case has been telegraphed by the Hubei Provincial Government to the central party headquarters and the Ministry of Transportation for consultation. Before receiving a reply from the central government, the union should wait quietly and must not take any action beyond regulations." The garrison headquarters simultaneously reported to the Three Provinces Bandit Suppression Headquarters and the Pacification Commissioner's Office that if a strike occurred and affected public security, the headquarters would only have emergency suppression measures to prevent the expansion of the dispute. Zhao Shusen and Lu Jingshi, standing committee members of the National Postal Workers' General Union, came to Hankou to mediate. On the 10th, they arrived in Hankou by the Jianguo steamer. On the 11th, they began formal negotiations with the postmaster and issued the following statement: "We have been ordered to come to Hankou because the Hankou postal authorities do not recognize the union, which has caused disputes. We are willing to take a fair attitude to seek a peaceful resolution. The Hankou postal workers' union has been established for a long time. The responsible executive and supervisory committee members and all members are united in good faith and are gradually getting on track. Moreover, in April of this year, the Hankou Special Municipality Party Headquarters clearly ordered the union to be registered, and the municipal government also had a clear statement of recognition. This provides a legal basis. The Hankou postmaster's failure to recognize the union is a result of improper handling, which has triggered a wave of unrest. We believe that the postal authorities should bear full responsibility for the creation of this incident. In today's serious national crisis, when the postal industry needs to be developed urgently, the only way to make progress is to strengthen cooperation between the bureau and the union. Moreover, the union's demands are extremely reasonable. The postal bureau should be open and honest. When we passed through Nanjing, we had earnest consultations with Minister of Transportation Zhu Jiahua and reached a satisfactory solution. The Hankou postal authorities must deeply recognize the reasonable demands of the union and must not

violate the general will of the people and deviate from the intentions of the party and government authorities, causing the matter to escalate and bear other unforeseen responsibilities." (September 11th)

Recently, Geng Dangzi entered and gathered to send the provincial government to Mengcheng to conduct a thorough investigation and capture. Japanese Actively Expanding Strength in the Northeast 105

Distressing Report from Jilin

The report made by a special envoy of the former Jilin Provincial Government, Mr. Cheng Yun, has already appeared in previous newspapers. Now we have obtained his latest report, which was forwarded by someone else. We have excerpted it as follows:

Actively Immigrating 106

Since Japan seized our Northeast, it has been actively implementing its immigration policy in order to completely occupy the Northeast with Japanese forces and, as the population gradually increases, to force our people to have no place to stand. The first immigrants are Japanese, and the second are Koreans. Most of the immigrants are in the counties of Jilin, Yanji, Wangqing, Shulan, Dunhua, etc., where Koreans are in the majority. Japanese immigrants are mostly in Yilan, Tongjiang, and other counties. It is said that there are also large numbers of colonists in the counties of Liaoning Province, but there are not many colonists in Heilongjiang Province at present. The areas where Japanese immigrants live in the Northeast are all armed with weapons, such as heavy artillery, machine guns, bullets, pistols, etc., to prevent attacks by the Volunteer Army. All Japanese immigrants who have moved into the country have the right to lease land and the right to freely purchase land.

Seizing Real Power 107

Currently, all real power in the puppet organization, such as finance, railways, and electricity, is in the hands of the Japanese.

Wherever Japanese power can reach, it penetrates everywhere. In terms of administration, a Japanese councillor is placed in each department. In terms of police administration, a guidance officer is placed. The great power of the puppet officials has been weakened and they are always subject to restrictions. Regarding the currency system, the puppet currency made in Japan is used uniformly, and the people are forced to use it. There is also a so-called Central Bank that issues various amounts of paper money indiscriminately. Today, it is difficult to see Chinese silver dollars and banknotes in large commercial ports or small villages and towns. As a result, commerce is not thriving everywhere. Except for Jilin, Changchun, and Harbin, where the situation is slightly better due to special circumstances, the situation is bleak everywhere else.

Anesthetizing the Masses 108

Japan is using the psychology of the Chinese people and loudly advocating the so-called "Royal Way Politics" in the Northeast, saying that true Royal Way Politics will only be seen again in the Northeast in the future. It is also using education as a means of assimilation, adding many hours of Japanese language instruction to all primary and secondary schools, while Chinese characters are listed as an elective subject. In May and July of this year, students from the First Normal School and the First Middle School in Jilin distributed anti-Japanese and national salvation leaflets. The Japanese discovered this and arrested more than thirty students from the two schools, executed more than ten, and the rest were sentenced to lengthy prison terms by the puppet court.

Eliminating Strength 109

The self-government organs of counties, districts, and villages in the Northeast have been completely disbanded by the Japanese. Now they are reimplementing the confiscation of civilian weapons, so that the people in the Northeast will never have the power to resist. As for the puppet army, it is mostly reorganized from the troops and bandits disbanded in the Northeast. The so-called Dingguo Army, Huguo Army, and Weiguo Army were disarmed by the Japanese army near Rehe. Currently, the most powerful army of rebels is Zhang Haipeng's army, followed by Yu Zhishan's and Ji Xing's puppet garrison brigades, puppet Jing'an guerrilla teams, and puppet railway guard teams, totaling about 300,000. Since July 1 of this year, Japan has been confiscating a regiment from each brigade of the puppet army. The puppet Jing'an guerrilla team and the puppet railway guard team have each had a company confiscated. The puppet officials who have been disarmed remain in the service of the upper-level Japanese department, still receiving their original salaries, while the soldiers are dismissed. The Japanese army stationed in the Northeast is mostly located in Manzhouli, Suifenhe, and the border areas of Tongren, etc. There are not many stationed in the provinces, cities, and counties. There are about 200 people in Jilin City. Japanese military aircraft fly to various places every day for inspection. At night, there are also aircraft flying in the air over Changchun City to detect movements.

People Have No Means of Livelihood 110

This year, due to favorable weather conditions from spring to summer, the autumn harvest is excellent, especially in Liaoning. The Japanese are all delighted, thinking that they will have land and wealth from now on. However, in reality, it is only the Chinese people who suffer. Taking Jilin Province as an example, since it was invaded and occupied by Japan, all 42 counties have been troubled and uneasy. The worst of these are Panshi, Huadian, and the remote counties in the northeast. According to the land in Panshi County, 80% of it cannot be cultivated because most of the residents have fled elsewhere.

War Originates from Economics 111

Malai Broadcasts a Speech Advocating Anti-War Principles

The Damei Evening News reports that Lord Malai, the leader of the European representatives of the Anti-War Congress, gave a speech on the principles of the Anti-War Congress on the China Broadcasting Corporation radio station last night (the 12th), which was translated into Chinese and broadcasted successively. The main points of his speech clarified that force cannot solve problems, but will only create other problems that are more difficult to solve. Throughout history, wars have all raised the false mask of self-defense, but in reality, they all originate from economics. The reason why various countries are opposed to the anti-war conference is because they fear that once the inside story of their policies is revealed, they will become the target of attacks from all over the world. This kind of universal evil psychology can be seen in Japan's opposition to the conference. The Japanese are doing their best to oppose it because they fear that their Manchurian policy will be criticized at the conference. In addition, France is opposed to the conference because it fears the exposure of its financial expansion policy and its ambition towards Yunnan. The United States is opposed to the conference because it fears that its policy of promoting trade through missionaries will be noticed. Britain is also unwilling to see the success of the conference because it fears that its interests in Tibet will be valued by others.

A Recent Glimpse of Land Prices in Shanghai 117

Land Prices Soar in the French Concession's Avenue Joffre Area

Land Prices in the Northern and Southern Districts are Depressed, with the Western District Expected to Rise

The Central News Agency reports that land prices in Shanghai have fluctuated greatly due to the impact of the January 28th Incident. In order to understand the land price situation in the city, the National Federation of Commerce has specially requested Mr. Pan Wen'an of the China Credit Information Bureau to conduct a personal investigation. The reporter was shown the investigation report by Mr. Pan yesterday. Excerpts are as follows. The investigations of various industries in Shanghai after the war, which were published in various newspapers yesterday, were also conducted by Mr. Pan.

Two Concessions 118

The areas where land prices in Shanghai have risen the fastest are Avenue Joffre, Route Conty, and Route Cardinal Mercier in the French Concession, and Avenue Edward VII in the British Concession. Today, it is difficult to purchase not only large pieces of land in these areas, but also small, scattered pieces. This is because the market in this area has suddenly flourished in recent years, and tram transportation has been expanded, so the sharp rise in land prices is to be expected. In the vicinity of Nanjing Road and Jing'an Temple Road in the British Concession, the market has been prosperous for many years, and land prices have risen to a considerable extent, so it seems unlikely that there will be another sharp increase. It is said that the Public Works Department plans to formulate a unified land price list to prohibit free increases.

Northern and Southern Districts 119

In the Chinese areas, such as Dongmen Road in Xiaodongmen and Heping Road in Ximen, the rate of increase has also been rapid. The triangular wasteland next to the Chen Yingshi Memorial Tower in Ximen, with an area of only seven or eight mu, sold for as much as 300,000 taels. However, the situation in the city is different from that in the concessions. Whenever the situation is slightly affected, the residents of the Chinese area tend to move to the concessions. At that time, the real estate prices in the Chinese area will immediately show a downward trend. During the Japanese invasion of Shanghai, traffic inside and outside the border was cut off for as long as two months, and land prices in the Chinese area suddenly fell sharply. Since the signing of the armistice agreement, land prices have rebounded slightly, but most buyers are still hesitant and unwilling to move forward. This is the main reason for the recent depression in the real estate industry in the Chinese area. Due to the past war disasters, land transactions in Zhabei are very scarce, so there is no formal market price. It is said that it is at least 30% to 40% lower than before the war. The land near Zhangjia Lane on Wuhua Road used to be worth five or six thousand taels per mu, but now it is worth four or five thousand taels, which is not very different. However, in the area along Yongxing Road, the price has dropped from three or four thousand taels to only two thousand taels. Recently, there have been transactions in the bustling area along Baoshan Road, but the price paid is also 30% to 40% lower than before the war. However, west of Meiyuan Road, the land price has only decreased to a limited extent compared to before the war.

Eastern and Western Districts 120

In the year before the January 28th Incident, factories sprang up in Yangshupu like mushrooms after a rain, and land prices soared. Land prices in the central district also increased significantly, but slightly less than in the eastern district. The western district did not show much progress in the first half of the twentieth year. Since the opening of negotiations on the construction of roads across the border, domestic and foreign attention has been focused on this area, which is considered to be the only area for expansion. Moreover, after the General Assembly purchased Xiangmao Villa, the neighboring landowners thought that the time had come, so they raised the land prices. In fact, transactions were very scarce. This year, land prices in the western district are still firm, while transactions in the eastern district are still few, and all are buying factory sites without speculation. Since the signing of the Tanggu Agreement, there has been a slight increase in activity. From the perspective of the overall trend, the rise in land prices in the area will eventually be realized sooner or later. There are four reasons for this: (1) The construction of the municipal government building has been completed. If the city center construction plan can be implemented step by step, land prices will inevitably rise. (2) After the increase in tariffs on imported goods, imports will decrease. Chinese people are gradually thinking of setting up factories to manufacture goods that were previously imported from overseas. Foreign companies are also planning to set up factories in China to manufacture due to the increased tariffs and high costs. The only suitable location for setting up factories is the eastern district. (3) Since the signing of the Tanggu Agreement, the relationship between China and Japan has gradually eased. Japanese companies are also planning to set up factories in China to avoid transportation problems. The location is also in the Jiangwan area. (4) The two-railway stations are planned to be moved to Jiangwan to connect with the port. If this can be realized, the land prices in the vicinity will definitely rise.

Cai Yuanpei and Others Telegraph to Request Protection of the Yungang Grottoes in Datong 121

The Yungang Grottoes in Datong were built in the early years of the Wei Dynasty and took more than 100 years to complete, with more than 10,000 stone Buddhas. Each of the larger ones is more than forty zhang tall, magnificent and solemn, and treasured by the world. They are a unique achievement in the history of art in our country. Recent reports say they have been destroyed by Zhao Chengzhou's troops. Cai Yuanpei, Ye Gongchao, and Liu Haisu of the Chinese Archaeological Society telegraphed Yan Xishan yesterday, saying, "To Mr. Yan Xishan of Taiyuan, Shanxi: Reports say the Yungang Grottoes in Datong have been destroyed by Commander Zhao Chengzhou's troops. It is regrettable that world-renowned antiquities are being destroyed in this way. Please strictly order their protection and restoration and prohibit any infringement. Yours sincerely, Cai Yuanpei, Ye Gongchao, Liu Haisu, et al. of the Chinese Archaeological Society."

Statistics on China's Exports to the United States for Seven Months of This Year 129

According to statistics released today (the 13th) by the US Consulate General, as reported by the Da Mei Evening News, China's exports to the United States in July were still largest in the category of inedible animals and their products, valued at US$1,174,278. These goods include leather, furs, bones, horns, bristles, feathers, ivory, etc. The total value for the seven months of this year was US$7,488,766, accounting for approximately 40% of the total export value. In addition, edible animals and their products exported to the US in July were only valued at US$83,224, which was the result of slow sales of egg powder. Edible plant products were valued at US$264,450, inedible plant products were valued at US$763,152, textile materials and textiles, which were previously top-ranked, fell to US$730,098, wood and paper were valued at US$8,115, non-metallic minerals were valued at US$23,842, metals and their products were valued at US$96,497, chemical products were valued at US$4,434, and miscellaneous items were valued at US$5,740. The total value of exports to the United States in July was US$4,162,738, and the total value for the seven months of this year was US$18,798,066.

National Goods Should Use Chinese Descriptions 130

The Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau yesterday instructed the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, saying: "According to an order from the Ministry of Industry, the Hankou Municipal National Goods Movement Committee reported that Standing Committee Member Wang Heqing stated that most trademarks of domestic factory products are described in English, making it difficult to distinguish national goods from foreign goods, which has a significant impact on the sales of national goods. It is proposed that the Ministry of Industry forward this to the provincial and municipal governments, ordering all manufacturers that, in the future, products sold domestically should uniformly use the national language, while those sold abroad should use Chinese as the main language and foreign languages for translation, in order to uphold the national system and facilitate identification. The indiscriminate use of English mixes domestic and foreign goods, making it impossible to distinguish national goods, which has a significant impact on promoting national goods and expanding production and sales. Therefore, all national goods sold domestically in the future should quickly switch to using Chinese descriptions to show distinction and facilitate sales." Therefore, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau orders the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to instruct all national goods factories to comply. This order is hereby issued.

Resolution of the Fuxin Factory's Lease of Railway Bureau Spur Track Case 135

Signing of Nine Supplementary Contracts

Contract Valid for Ten Years - Xin Xin News Agency reports that in the autumn of the fifteenth year of the Republic, the Fuxin Flour Mill requested the Railway Bureau to lay a spur track from the three-mile point of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway to the front of the factory's freight station on Xiaoshadu Road for its lease. The Railway Bureau built it, and on December 1 of that year, the two parties signed a contract with fourteen clauses. However, disputes arose soon after implementation, causing losses to both sides. Now, the Railway Bureau believes that the prolonged delay of this case not only affects railway revenue but also violates the purpose of the railway to circulate goods. After detailed consideration, on the 5th of this month, it signed nine supplementary contracts with the Fuxin Flour Mill to resolve the issue. A Xin Xin News Agency reporter has recorded the contracts signed before and after the case and the process as follows:

Original Contract 136

Contractors: Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration (hereinafter referred to as the "Railway Bureau"), Fuxin Flour Mill (hereinafter referred to as the "Fuxin Factory"). The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration has approved the request of the Fuxin Flour Mill to build a branch line to reach the factory and has stipulated the following rules: (1) The branch line shall start from the three-mile point of the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway and reach the outside of the Fuxin Factory. The Railway Bureau shall be responsible for the construction, and the Fuxin Factory shall be allowed to use the branch line in accordance with the following regulations. (2) The Fuxin Factory shall pay 3,000 silver dollars for various expenses of the Railway Bureau in building the branch line on the factory's land, such as filling earth, ditches, labor costs, and supervision fees for managing this work. All materials required for building the branch line shall be borrowed and repaired by the Railway Bureau in accordance with the provisions of Article 3. (3) The Railway Bureau shall charge 12% of the original value of the building materials borrowed by the Fuxin Factory each year as rent. This fee shall include annual road maintenance fees and shall be collected starting from the date of completion of the road. (4) The Fuxin Factory shall deposit 5,000 silver dollars with the Railway Bureau. This amount shall be refunded by the Railway Bureau when the freight value of the branch line reaches 20,000 yuan per year. At any time, if the Fuxin Factory does not continue to use this branch line and the freight value has not reached the above amount, the deposit shall be forfeited by the Railway Bureau, and all materials shall be retrieved by the Railway Bureau. (5) In addition to freight and other fees that shall be paid in accordance with regulations, each car entering the branch line shall be charged a switching fee based on the car's capacity, calculated from the starting point of the branch line, at 2.5 cents per ton per kilometer. (6) The collection of fees for vehicle and tarpaulin delays shall be in accordance with the regulations of the Railway Bureau. (7) At any time, if there are empty spaces on the branch line, the Railway Bureau shall have the right to use them for dispatching vehicles. (8) The Railway Bureau shall have the right to lay other branch lines to connect with this branch line if it deems it feasible. (9) The Railway Bureau and the Fuxin Factory shall each be responsible for losses incurred by either party's staff due to negligence or errors in performing their duties on the branch line and shall bear the compensation for the party suffering the loss. (10) The Fuxin Factory shall hand over the cars loaded with goods waiting to be transported on the branch line to the Railway Bureau at the time designated by the Railway Bureau. (11) If the Railway Bureau deems it necessary, the Fuxin Factory shall build gates and fences at the boundary of the Railway Bureau in accordance with the instructions of the Railway Bureau's engineer for protection purposes. (12) During the validity period of the contract, the Fuxin Factory shall transport all of its goods through the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureau. This transportation shall be in the name of the Fuxin Flour Mill and shall not be handled by a transportation company. (13) If the Fuxin Flour Mill fails to make payments on time and exceeds the deadline by more than 30 days, the Railway Bureau shall have the right to seize the factory's goods and other movable property on the branch line in accordance with the law to compensate for the loss. (14) The contract shall be valid for ten years. After that, the Railway Bureau or the Fuxin Factory shall make other regulations twelve months before the expiration of the contract.

Course of the Dispute 137

The above contract was signed by Fuxin First Factory, but at the time, the factory's original intention was to include Maoxin and Shenxin factories. The branch track was also shared by the three factories. However, according to Article 12 of the contract, it seemed that other than Fuxin, Maoxin and Shenxin were not applicable. Therefore, disputes arose soon after implementation. Later, workers on Maigen Road, on the pretext that the goods transported into the branch track did not belong to Fuxin First Factory, forcibly detained them at the Maizhan station, preventing them from being dropped into the branch track for unloading, resulting in a major dispute. Fuxin Factory's one-time loss reached more than 7,000 yuan. Subsequently, in the 19th and 20th years of the Republic, it repeatedly requested the Railway Bureau to amend the contract, but it remained unresolved for a long time. The goods of the Fuxin, Maoxin, and Shenxin factories were all switched to waterway transportation to Shanghai. At the same time, the rent for the branch track was also stopped, accumulating to more than 6,700 yuan to date. Repeated demands for payment were met with the excuse that the Railway Bureau refused to amend the contract and that the branch track was useless, so payment was refused. The Railway Bureau believes that the prolonged delay of this case not only affects railway revenue but also violates the purpose of the railway to circulate goods. After detailed consideration, it believes that (1) the branch track has been invested in and built by the railway and should be fully utilized to directly facilitate passenger transport for loading and unloading goods and indirectly develop the social economy and regulate people's livelihoods; (2) the contract conditions should be based on mutual benefit; (3) in order to save the declining freight transport, the railway should work with major industrialists to promote progress. Based on this purpose, it began negotiations with Fuxin Factory in March of this year and drafted nine supplementary contracts, which were submitted to the Ministry of Railways for approval. However, considering that the current freight transport is in decline, after detailed consultation, it was proposed to use the branch track to attract freight transport for the railway, and the fifth supplementary contract was supplemented. All merchant goods are not restricted from loading and unloading on the branch track. Subsequently, instructions were received to approve the supplementary measures for a one-year trial. With the consent of the Fuxin Flour Mill, it was officially signed and established on September 5. The Railway Bureau then issued a written certificate of the supplementary measures and notified the Traffic and Accounting Departments. At this point, the case was finally concluded. The signed clauses of the supplementary contracts are published below:

Supplementary Clauses 138

Contractors: Jinghu Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration (hereinafter referred to as the "Railway Bureau"), Fuxin Flour Mill (hereinafter referred to as the "Fuxin Factory"). With the consent of both parties, the supplementary clauses to the contract signed on December 1 of the 15th year of the Republic are hereby stipulated as follows: Article 1: The Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration mentioned in the original contract shall be changed to the Jinghu Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration from the date of signing of this supplementary contract. Article 2: The Fuxin Flour Mill mentioned in the original contract shall be changed to the Maofu Shenxin Company from the date of signing of this supplementary contract. Article 3: Upon expiration of the contract, the 5,000 yuan deposit previously paid by the Fuxin Factory to the Railway Bureau shall be refunded by the Railway Bureau in one lump sum upon presentation of the receipt. If the factory does not continue to use this branch line, all railway materials on the branch line shall be recovered by the Railway Bureau. Article 4: The distance from Maigen Road to the inside of the branch track shall be calculated as two kilometers, and a switching fee of 2.5 cents per ton per kilometer shall be charged. Article 5: In order to promote the business development of both parties, any flour raw materials transported to Maofu Shenxin Company, essential supplies for the company's factory, or products of the company transported to any merchant* shall be loaded and unloaded on the branch track. Article 6: Maofu Shenxin Company shall transport as much of its own materials and products as possible through these two railways. Article 7: In addition to the clauses stipulated in the contract, all other relevant railway regulations shall be observed. Article 8: All clauses in the original contract, except for the names of the two parties and Articles 4, 5, 12, and 13 of the regulations, which shall be subject to the amended clauses, shall remain in effect. Article 9: This supplementary contract shall take effect from the date of signing. Upon expiration of the original contract (ten years from December 1, 15th year of the Republic), this supplementary contract shall expire accordingly. Jinghu Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration, Fuxin Flour Mill, September 5, 22nd year of the Republic of China.

Bei Songsun Lectures on the Silver Issue 139

Invited by the International Issues Research Association

Mr. Bei Songsun of the Bank of China accompanied Minister Song to various countries in Europe and America to attend the World Economic Conference and made remarkable achievements. He has now returned to Shanghai after completing his duties. The International Issues Research Association specially invited Mr. Bei to lecture on the silver issue at the Bank Club at 5:00 PM on the 11th of this month. Guo Bingwen, Zou Bingwen, Xu Xinliu, Chen Liting, Li Zhaohuan, Cao Yunxiang, Chen Zheqing, and members Cai Wuji, Lin Kanghou, Xu Jilong, Wu Liande, Chen Lingyi, Huang Renzhi, and dozens of others attended. Chairman Guo Bingwen first stood up to give a speech, saying in brief: "It is a great honor to have Mr. Bei present today to give a lecture. Mr. Bei accompanied Minister Song to attend the World Economic Conference and worked extremely hard. I would like to express my condolences on behalf of this association and ask Mr. Bei to share his experiences abroad to increase the knowledge of my colleagues." Bei then thanked him and began his lecture on the silver issue. His speech was as follows: We want to

discuss the silver issue 140

we must first talk about the reasons for the drop in silver prices. There are only two reasons for this: first, it is related to politics, and second, it is due to the recession. We know that when silver prices rise, commodity prices rise accordingly, and when silver prices fall, commodity prices also fall. This is because although silver is one type of commodity, it is still used as currency in several countries. However, this rule may sometimes change, such as in the special circumstances of the European War. However, silver prices are always

a barometer of commodity prices 141

In 1896, the United States also experienced a major turmoil due to the recession. At that time, Pola Boyal advocated the free minting of gold and silver coins, with a ratio of silver to gold of sixteen to one, and the Democratic presidential candidate referred to it as the Free Coinage Campaign. Later, in 1899, people began to feel the shortage of gold. According to the report of the League of Nations Gold Committee, if the gold mines of Alaska had not been discovered, the world's gold would have been insufficient to allocate. After the European War, countries worked hard to increase production, but at first, due to wartime losses, everyone tried to replenish supplies, and goods still had a market. Later, more and more goods accumulated, and commodity prices also fell. So everyone tried to push the goods abroad, causing

international trade war 142

leading to the global recession we see today. Secondly, why are silver prices related to politics? Since the United Kingdom reduced the silver content of its subsidiary coins, countries have followed suit. India also imitated it from 1926 based on the report of the Royal Commission of that year. It gradually withdrew the Robi circulating in the market and successively sold off its silver bullion reserves. Between 1929 and 1932, silver prices fell uncontrollably. At that time,

had a great impact on our country 143

Economic research conclusion

As a result, it was proposed to prohibit the import of silver, but in order to maintain international trade, our government expressed its opposition. However, at that time, a letter was sent to the Indian government, hoping that they would change their silver sales policy. At the same time, the year with the highest silver production was 1929, with as much as 262.2 million ounces. On the one hand, due to the recession, the sales of silver decreased. On the other hand, due to the sales by various governments and the increase in silver production, silver prices naturally fell further and further, and the voice of maintaining silver prices became higher and higher. The American people seem to have a special affection for silver. In fact, the amount of silver produced in the United States is still below that of Mexico. It is said that it is due to

historical relationship 144

became a kind of superstition, so it was taken very seriously at this meeting, and opinions from experts were sought in many ways. As a result, it was felt that there was a real need to maintain silver prices. At the London conference, the United States proposed three steps to maintain silver prices. First, currency should still be used gold. The second way is to save the use of gold. Countries using gold can only use gold as a reserve and for insufficient international trade. On one side, recover gold stored by the people. Those who must use gold for industry must apply to the government for permission and purchase it from the market. The delivery must be made through the central banks of various countries. Third, the central bank's cash reserve is reduced to 25%, of which 20% is used for gold and 5% can be used for silver, but the silver purchased should be equal to other commodity prices. This plan is very much related to maintaining silver prices.

As for currency inflation 145

although to raise commodity prices

one of the strategies, but if there is no actual market for various goods, the price increase will be temporary and contains great dangers. In the Washington talks, the United States had already discussed this plan with several countries. Although there was generally no objection, countries such as Britain and France felt that the addition of silver to the reserve still needed to be considered. In terms of raising silver prices, there were two sides to the debate at the time. One side thought it would affect our country's exports, and the other side thought it would benefit our country and increase purchasing power. The US authorities questioned our country's representatives at the time, and the answer at the time was that if commodity prices rise, silver prices will naturally rise, but it is hoped that silver prices will not be higher than all commodity prices, and the principle is to be equivalent to general commodity prices, and at the same time, it is hoped that there will be a way to stabilize silver prices. The silver issue is in,
